A TV anime would be much more expensive because:

1) It would be much longer resulting into higher costs in every department
2) The whole thing needs far more management because you can't just put something on TV out of nothing
3) You don't do a TV show only for the sake of having a TV show - You need partners in many departments to get the best out of it

A TV anime that does LWA justice would probably cost a few millions.

Why do people unironically do this retarded "LWA IS AN ANTI-OTAKU ANTI-FANSERVICE WORK" stuff, especially when the anime staff themselves drew stuff like pic related and this and the manga ran in a seinen magazine? I'm not saying the show isn't kid-friendly, but to act like the staff didn't intend the characters to be cute and attractive to nerds is ridiculous. Fuck, even mainstream TV stuff really obviously marketed at kids tends to make sure to draw the characters in an attractive way to appeal to fanboys & fangirls, so to expect Trigger to take that stance would be insane.

The "westaboo anime" stuff is wrong too. LWA is a million times more anime-esque than Panty & Stocking, and Panty & Stocking itself was far more anime-esque than people claim in spite of the colossal western cartoon influences.

It's true that Yoshinari is a "westaboo" in that he even worships stuff that English-speaking cartoon nerds don't give a fuck about like Atomic Betty, but LWA is not a "westaboo" work in itself at all. It simply uses principles associated with good ANIMATION in general; just because those animation principles first came about in the west and were written down by Disney doesn't mean they are "westaboo", as pretty much all well-animated anime with "cartoony" aesthetics use them. LWA itself is no more "westaboo" than FLCL.

Studio Trigger teased a new project, its fourth major project, at its Anime Expo panel on Thursday. It showed preliminary designs of several school students as well as a verdant city in the sea, intersected with bridges. The staff members added that the project has yet to be announced in Japan. Studio Trigger also showed an Inferno Cop short with a crossover with Little Witch Academia characters. The staff said that the short has yet to premiere in Japan.

There is nothing "Americanized" about LWA. It's a very well-made anime. The problem is you've associated actual good character designs and animation as "western", and you think anime is defined by being generic shit.




Why are none of you bringing up the fact that LWA is extremely anime-like? The designs are anime as fuck, it's just appealingly-drawn anime. The standards of cartoon "appeal" were defined by Americans, but ALL good-looking anime use them. LWA is no more "westaboo" than FLCL; both have western media references but both are largely very anime-like.

Yoshinari is also a huge fan of Osamu Tezuka; people also say Tezuka works are "western cartoon style" but they're not, they took western influences but utilized them in a uniquely Japanese way. In fact, Tezuka style is the purest form of the "traditional anime" aesthetic and the best-looking "traditional anime" is made by people who understand what Tezuka created on a deeper level than the average artist.

The way some people simplify the complexity of Tezuka's style and plentiful influences to "he draws like Disney, lol" is silly as fuck.

"Disney" as a studio are not a hivemind. Tezuka may have taken Bambi's eyes, but his overall style is not at all like that of Bambi. He was more overtly influenced by Carl Barks' Donald Duck comics, but that's only part of it. Fleischer animation clearly played a colossal part, at least their early work from before they tried to rip off Looney Tunes and Disney; he liked Popeye so much that he inserted him in his Monkey King manga.

Yoshinari's "normal anime" art looks so fucking appealing and good because he understands the foundation of the aesthetic. Dude's a big Tezuka fan.

Anime cuteness is very different from western cartoon cuteness and comparing LWA to 90s Disney style is the most surface-level and shallow thing.

Look at how Tezuka drew a 'cute cartoon bunny girl' design vs. how a Disney film did it. Anime cuteness is far more focused on the bare impression than the details. Takashi Murakami (I think) once made the point that a cartoon cat in the west is "a drawing of a cat", while Japan's Hello Kitty feels like "a drawing of a drawing of a cat". That's a fantastic way of wording it.

semi auto reloads semi automatically
you pull the trigger and it shoots, you pull again and it has reloaded and shoots one bullet again

full auto means the reloading cycle will work and therefor the gun will shoot until you let the trigger go or it runs out of ammo

no auto means you have to manually reload after every shot, bolt action etc

Manual = 1 trigger pull, 1 shot, 1 reload, 1 trigger pull, 1 shot, 1 reolad, etc

Semi-Auto = 1 trigger pull, 1 shot, 1 trigger pull, 1 shot, etc, 1 reload, etc

Full Auto: 1 trigger hold, X amount of shots, 1 reload, 1 trigger hold, X amount of shots, 1 reload, etc

Sorry but no. It was exactly the same thing. The fans of both shows spammed threads for the sheer fun of seeing the pages flooded with threads. It was great fun if you were a fan of either show, but very obnoxious if you weren't. I'm guessing that as a fan of CG, you were probably blind to the other side of it all. After the second season of CG, in late 08 and throughout most of 09, meta threads were very popular, possibly triggered by increasing amounts of spammers, downtimes, and the like, people talked at length about whether or not the board was becoming irreversibly shit or not. And in those threads, you saw lots of people voicing unfavourable opinion about what happened to the board culture in the wake of very popular shows like CG or TTGL.

https://youtu.be/Lghg0-H1-CM [ ]
It all ties into the series' musical references, and how Bob Fosse once said that most songs are either "I Am" songs or "I Want" songs. Normal stands are like "I Am" songs, which are about the character's personality, job, or role in the story. Requiem stands are like "I Want" songs; they are about desires and goals.

There are also "I Am Becoming" songs, which tend to mix aspects of "I Am" and "I Want" songs. Typically they're about how someone is growing as a person or how they're achieving their goals and desires. Stands with multiple "Acts" like Tusk are like "I Am Becoming" songs
